Coming back to our discussion trail - Matt thanks for the refence to the notes on Nature OF Order. However for some one who is waiting to read the original,I shall not recommend it. I think CA invites the reader to explore and he builds up certain concepts through illustrations and empirical evidence which will influence the reader in some way or the other ,and by reading the note before hand might spoil some of the charm. This is of course purely personal feeling. Ofcourse such notes will be handy reference after the reading. The other work on Poetry seems interesting , hopefully I shall get some time to go deeper into it.
Now to Vaskos question : why do not I want to get into psychological probing? Well I do want to get into psychological probing in the sense of exploring the role of Patterns in the human mind. What I was saying before was in reference to my approach or my model- I was narrating why I brought up the model-the reason was not to do the psychological probing but to get an handle of the bigger picture first -then the whole practical utility of such a model would be all sorts of implication at the social interaction level and also of course at the personal feeling level. But such a consequence will be a bit different from what is the dominant established practise in the field of psychology today.
Coming to the field of personal feeling and our egos, they certainly have a very very constructive role to play in every thing we do and perceive. My position with the "Scene" is it allows a person's every minute perception about the outside world and also his/her inside world to lay bare in uniform snapshots of time. As you can imagine there will be millions of such scenes [in theory] and there the computer comes handy. I shall talk a bit more about it shortly. But another aspect of the scene is it captures the stillness of the person in question.. It allows him to detach himself from the immediate attention needed to carry out a task but still be very mind-full of every detail that is being carried out moment by moment. Actually, one of the 15 fundamental rules by CA is 'Roughness' and there he talks about how a state of mind he calls "egolessness" which allows a person to let the "regularity or order of a situation to let loose".
Now, in my view what happens in the computer is it [the computer] goes through millions and millions of scenes to do a task while carrying the measures[measures meaning values held by keypoints] from one scene to the other. This fundamental affair in the computer remains hidden and packaged by the social and technical process that is setup to make and use a software package. It is not so difficult to bring back and leverage off the fundamental process that is going on -just that we have to re-orient ourselves how we make the computers work. Of-course this will be a complete re-reorientation. -Looking for centers around program or documentation code will not achieve it. Beauty of the centers and all the 15 rules is that they can act at various scales-my beleif is the life in software can be brought about by working on centers created by the actions and behaviour that both the developers [several layers of developers] and the users (hence the community in general) induce themselves to by using the computer. I am not ruling out the possibilty of finding centers around program codes -but those centers will be very weak inconsequential centers.

Matt Farrelly 02:06:39 4/23/2002
Hi everyone,
I assume from the title of Christopher Alexander's new book "The Nature Of Order" that he is saying something in some way about the fundamental laws if the universe, that there is some pattern to the way all natural structures are formed at all levels. Whether it be the physical properties of materials, the cellular structure of a living organism or the structure of human perception and thought. If so that theory has the potential to apply to all the things we are talking about whether it be from building architecture, software development, art and permaculture.

Pronob, you said that he proposed 15 fundamental rules for structure. I haven't read CA's book yet but I have read some interesting commentaries by Richard Gabriel who has done a lot of work with patterns in the software development field. He provides a good introduction to Alexander’s concepts for those, like me, who have not yet been able to get hold of the original work. If you are interested you can read the paper at http://www.dreamsongs.com/NewFiles/NatureOfOrder.pdf. He also has another paper that I found even more interesting where he used CA’a 15 rules to analyse the structure of a number of poems especially “The Second Coming” by W. B. Yeats and others. His intention was to see if see if the 15 rules or properties could be used to help create better poetry. And I must say that in reading his analysis I certainly found that the properties helped me understand why one poem could be though of as more beautiful or profound than another and where one poem was weak or strong. You can read this paper at http://www.dreamsongs.com/NewFiles/NatureOfPoeticOrder.pdf.

It seems to me that if Christopher Alexander’s proposed properties of living structures could be applied successfully to poetry, a field for which they were not specifically designed, then there is every chance that they could be applied to many other fields. Including of course the search for good patterns in building and architecture but also possibly software development and permaculture. You could argue that poetry is mainly concerned with form, whereas these other fields are concerned also with function to a greater or lesser degree. So it will be interesting to find out how well CA’s ideas apply to the function side of the equation.

I’m interested to hear if anyone else has read any of Richard Gabriel’s commentaries and what were your thoughts.

Matt

Pronob Pal 22:01:46 4/22/2002
Goodday Everyone,
Vasko,
I can very well appreciate the difficulty in relating to my model. For that reason I propose to digress a little and have some more light hearted discussion about how I came to the point of my understanding and also probably what I want to achieve. You have also rightly pointed out the absence of the right exposure about the model in my site. This has been in my tasklist, and it was there at the site before I changed the site in preparation for a more global approach –thru arts, literature and science into Patterns. But that has not happened mainly owing to lack of interest from any one else. Also because this has been a totally un-funded [or self-funded] part-time activity these can easily go to a lower priority unless one takes a pretty mercenary attitude towards it.
Now coming back to my model, I proposed it first time in a series of articles in 1991-1992 in the KeyWord journal of the NSW Association for Technical and Scientific Communication. The model was proposed as architecture for technical writing. Probably that was a start in the wrong footing, because technical communication is only the documentation aspect of software technology. The fact that I am taking a different approach-where the documentation is spawned as part of the computation model and not as an optional adjunct did not reach the right audience. What I proposed was that the process of understanding and computation can be seen as one and the same if and only if we take the right base for our computation. Since then, during the following 3 years I developed a software-package called Intention Analyst using an easy to program multimedia package called “ToolBook”. I had a free copy of this available at my site. I shall put that back again. The model that I have currently in my mind probably will not be truly reflected in that 7-year-old software package –but it will give you the option to set up your own patterns and scenes and do the tour of patterns. I was trying to sell Intention Analyst to business analysts who do the software specification, for doing requirement analysis. But this was also of no business success- need more dollar [more so in those days] and marketing to reach the high profile corporate IT market. In the next two weeks, I shall probably have a bit of time dedicated to updating my site and shall try to do those that I promised above.
Your question about Scene and Patterns is leading to the right answer. Mathematically as well, Patterns being a sequence of Scenes can be a sequence with just one member –in which case the pattern and the Scene coincide. Another point about my approach, I had kept an eye on the Pattern community works in the software field mainly through the published journal and books. I have not seen any scheme of using patterns as the drivers of software execution. This is one reason probably they find whatever I say as too new and untested or even flimsy. Recently I have been reading Christopher Alexander’s book on Nature of Order. I have been only half way through the first volume. Although I must admit I could not resist the temptation of reading ahead a chapter or two towards the end. I am moved by the possibilities he talks about- where form and function becomes a whole and also how around 15 rules at the generic level can cause a finished whole to emerge. I am biased, but I have a hunch that the model I have will converge nicely with some of his concepts. This is another reason I am glad you and others in this discussion are interested in my model because [assuming you will be interested in CA’s approach] you can be a critique when I talk about how my model can fit in the bigger picture of human activity outside software engineering field. I shall like to finish today with some musing about how I see a Scene. Actually recently I have realised my Scene concept itself is pretty non-standard. Scene in my model is a snapshot of reality. But this reality can also include a few mental abstract objects. Like when you are picturing an ATM machine at the street corner you are also picturing the customer account which is an abstract thing in the corner of the street. Also you asked why tourist. The tourist analogy probably emphasise the fact that when a human being is understanding a Scene we can assume he/she does not know anything in a Scene just like a tourist is ignorant about the activities in a new city. The other point in taking Scene as a mix of reality and mental objects is that it is a bit less arrogant approach and acknowledges the possibility that we human beings are also part of a bigger pattern which we probably not understand-at least not yet. You may ask how that is done? –Point I am making is our thought processes are generating or passing through Scenes at every moment, so a theory based on Scenes includes the behaviour [or mindset] of the person who is proposing or working with such a theory e.g. the person under the influence of known and unknown patterns. At the same time I don’t want to get into psychological probes either – I am interested in a more mathematical and somewhat 'whole-istic' approach –there I like CA’s approach. I have a belief if the nature of order extends to every artefact we build today it has surely some influence on how our mind exists in this whole world. Hopefully I can go to the foothills of such mystery oneday. Our new friend Matt's[Hello Matt] remark about genes is of course very true-my question though is more at the mind level.
Another question you asked : what is the working model of Patterns?. For that purpose I am restricting myself to software field. That will mean an internet based facility with a software-agent as the intermediary which allows 1. Developer to develop software 2. Users to use the software while the agent conducts dialogue by seraching through relevant patterns and prompting right intentions. This is trying to address the problem in design reuse I talked about before.
May be we shall take up the discussion of community interaction once we straighten out the pattern-scene role and the model. I feel they are very much related.
Talk to you soon
Thanks.

This seems to me to be one of the most important ideas in all of what Christopher Alexander is trying to say. That we need to break down our idealised view of nature as something separate and pure and instead bring it into our daily lives recognising that we will inevitably change it by our interactions but that these changes are not necessarily a bad thing. I think this theme is related to your other question Vasko about what working patterns are.

Pronob Pal 03:42:30 4/16/2002
Geogina and Vasko,
Thanks for your feed back. One point, the numbering can be done in any scattered way-as long as they maintian a sequence in this discussion-it need not be added to the same list-what do you think?
Starting from the patterns Vasko suggested let us put numbers like the following:
5.Sustaining Community Life
5.1 Lively Neighbourhoods
5.1.1 Neighbourly Interaction
5.1.1.1 Drinking with Friends
5.1.1.1.1 Art of Drinking
5.1.1.1.1.1 Art of WineMaking
5.1.1.1.1.1.1 Steps To Prepare Wine
5.1.1.1.1.2 Place to Drink
5.1.1.1.1.3 Retreat with Friends
6. The Art of Loosing Oneself in Different Cultures
6.1 Belief System and intoxication.
Why the patterns came out to be related like this? Because I am interested in a particular scene which will provide a place for making wine at your home where you not only make and store wine
but also entertain and celebrate and exchange ideas and tell stories,jokes and just go beyond ordinary every day routine work. So the pattern "drinking with Friends" will infact bring forth issues which go much beyond drinking for intoxication. It will probably explore possibility of being drunk without being intoxicated. It will
explore what the word "drunk" can really mean.Those issues will trickle down to the Art of Drinking where it will possibly talk about actual drinking styles-the type of bottle
and glass,table used and so on ,will come to type of place and structure where you feel comfortable with different variations of mood- different kinds of people. These will all add up to the disign of the wine cellar where for some mysterious reason every one loves to visit and share a bottle while you chat away about things in life.

The reason why the wine cellar became burrried in so deep nesting of Patterns is you wanted to link it with the pattern "Lively Neighbourhoods". The point I am making is firstly Pattern nesting is necessary to bring multiple aspects or issues play in the solution and secondly the way patterns are nested is very much dependent on the particular solution or "scene". Also point to remember patterns can influnce a scene without being nested in the hierarchy.e.g 5 and 6 above.


The relation ships between Scene and Patterns is very vital. The structure you are mentioning is relative to the Scene, where as each individual pattern has it own existance as a sequence of scenes.You are adding one scene to an existing sequences in every pattern so that each pattern still maintains a continuity in its own right through the focuses marked at every member scene. I have arrived at this model after studying the nature of science,problems,investigations and solutions and of many different aspects of life and human interaction. Scene has come out to me as real life snap shots that has no real boundaries. The cross between the
pattern and the scnes I call Focus is a collection of "key-points"-each being a phrase or a word and can be regarded as the smallest unit of understanding. Such key points can also have a measure or value associated with it. Scene can be physical world details or mental images or a mix of both. So by "real Life" I include both
real world and mental world almost in one breadth. Focus is one point of attention.
The fun starts when we build a computational model out of this picture-the analogy is to a travelling
tourist which represents human way of understanding things. As the tourist travels from one focus to another
on a pattern tour,the tourist builds a collection of keypoints similar to the way we human beings build up our background with experiences in real life [education included] and understanding.
So the model says you and I always learn and act through patterns and nothing but patterns but at the same time we act differently at each scene because our background is different. At each focus the tourist also invokes "intentions" which are either
questions or observations. Each such question or observation add keypoints to tourists collection aswell.
Ofcourse I am still to develop a fully working model of what I have said and
implement into todays software technology -where main practical outcome will be the availability of software that will have an agent between the user of the software and the developer of the software. This agent will have an idea of the user's background and the developers background and shall act as the bridge between the two by faciliatating some ride through the patterns which both user and developer understands. This will solve the problem of design reuse I spoke about before.
Hope you find this interesting.
Speak to you soon.
Thanks

Pronob Pal From Canberra, Australia

http://www.visualanalytics.com.au

vasko drogriski 03:08:27 4/13/2002
Hi everybody,

Pronob, thanks for your latest addition. What you are really talking about is the structure of pattern languages? l am trying to get a handle on your idea of how the scenes and patterns relate. l remember reading a paper by Nikos Salingaros on this subject. It was very much along these lines. Anyone interested can find his paper in his home page in his online books about architecture (if you haven't seen already).
l would propose that small, bite size articles like Salingaros's, as an example, could be topic papers for small study groups. These papers give good theoretical background to patterns ideas.
So, yes l am interested in the study groups.
Pronob, your compilation of patterns has also urged me to think about writing patterns, for this is what you are in essence doing and urging for us to do.
And, it has occured to me that my earlier talk about 're-discovering' or 'articulating' patterns from our communities, in essence really is the requirement for the skill to be able to write patterns.
Most of us live the patterns, even implement them in one way or another, whether we do it as professional designers or lay people going about our daily lives, re-arranging the furniture, building a fence, planting a vegetable garden, whatever. But writing the patterns is different.

Georgina your offer to host a conference, or at least a 'convergence'in your town, of interested people, sounds great. Some sort of convergence, or coming together would possibly concretise particular outcomes and pursuits for different people. It's just a matter of how and when. So if anyone would like to further the proposal, let's see what we can do.
l would be happy to play some role in facilitating the process of getting people together in 'real' space.

But, to get back to patterns, l would like to add some more patterns to Pronobs list. (l think they are patterns).

This morning, on my way to the market, l saw the first grapes coming to Melbourne. They come on trucks, delivered from various parts of country Victoria. People from the community come to these places where the trucks wait, every year, in autumn, groups of men, very early to buy the grapes to make wine at home with their friends.
Appart from the fact that this alone, constitutes a pattern of some sort- it brings to mind other patterns, some related and some not directly related to this one.
So my main pattern is 'sustaining community life' then 'lively neighbourhoods', with 'Making wine' as a sub pattern for this larger pattern.
Under 'lively neighbourhoods', there could be other, more specific, more focused patterns, like 'sharing food', 'helping with work', 'food production', then more specific, down to 'crushing grapes', 'bottling and storing the wine', all the way down to, (excuse the pun, no humor intended) 'wine cellar' which itself becomes a 'implementation' pattern. Here we design a wine cellar for the storage of the wine.

So, Pronob, l would like to try and add at least two patterns to your list. My guess is that 'lively neighbourhoods' should go somewhere amongst the first four, while 'sustaining community life', being more general, somewhere before the first four. 'Wine cellar' on the other hand might fit into ???
While the other patterns like 'sharing food', 'helping with work', 'making and bottling wine' might go under 2.?

What l have left out so far is where to make the wine. This is another 'implementation' pattern, that is, a pattern which manifests in a particular geometry of a space somewhere, where the pattern can happen. But this pattern, and its space is more difficult to define. It is more difficult because wine making is not the only thing (its one scene of many??), that sustains communities, makes neighbourhoods lively, or feeds people at the end of the day. There are other things like, making bread, collecting eggs, growing vegetables, roasting and storing capsicums, not to mention non-dietary needs, etc... and most often these things happen together or in different seasons throughout the year and within the geometry of the space of the neighbourhood or the immediate house. They overlap. So the space for making wine for exapmle must accomodate other activities which sustain the community. So, why do l find it more difficult to put my finger on this space, to find its definite spatial arrangement and character, while 'wine cellar' is easier?
l know the wine cellar, generally goes under the house, should be accessible from the area where the wine is made, but should not be too public or announce its entrance, it should be in a cool place, out of the sun etc. etc...
If l think back of all the times l saw wine being made, families coming together to make wine, l still can not define exactly what the character of the space was that allowed wine making for example to happen. Or put in another way, if someone asked me, 'design me a place where to make wine?' l would not know where to start. l would say, you can do it any where, outside in the yard, inside the garage, in the middle of the garden, anywhere, as long as there is enough space to 'swing a cat' you can set your stuff up there and make the wine. You don't need much space, or any specially arranged space, so far as l have been able to identify.
The same thing goes for other activities. Harvesting the last vegetables from that years garden, cooking them, storing them etc... They all happened, over and over again, year after year, season through season. Families came and went, friendships and relationships changed, but people in the community made wine, wether it was with the same family as last year or a new family, it happened.
l can't define the precise character of that space, but l can describe elements of it which made the making of wine and all the other acivities which sustain and make communities lively possible.
For example, most households had a vegetable garden, often there was a gate between the yards, and often the gate was in the vegetable garden, there was a outdoor kitchen, tap, some sort of gas stove or even outdoor wood oven, a covered area where everyone could sit out of the rain or in the shade, where you could push the hot heap of burning embers and coals out of the rain for the last few capsicums and on and on...
It's all very amorphous, and difficult to pin point at times.

Apologies for rambling, but its raining today and there's nothing else to do.

These patterns are also quite culturally specific, they come from peasant communities, cold climate, but l suppose they can also apply or be relevant to anyone who drinks wine, eats vegetables, grows food etc...

l would like to get to your other point Pronob about "how different sections of the community can interact to bring up a solution"...

At this stage however, l well pause for any responses to our discussions.

Talk to you again.

Pronob Pal 03:14:20 4/11/2002
Hello Everyone,
I was thrilled to look at the range of the discussions and proposed patterns.

Toby’s remark on the capitalisim as a pattern language is appealing. In fact I was thinking along similar line after reading Georgina's response. New pattern language will certainly evolve to give formation to new ..isms needed to replace capitalism. But in fact pattern language has something more powerful than any ..ism can deliver. That is because pattern language can bring in the dynamism bottom up and can allow multiple isms to coexist. That is why pattern languages are closer to life.
Also I have just received the first book in the Nature Of Order series. This is an extraordinarily revealing ,wonderfully rewarding & brilliantly entertaining book!!!
I shall treasure every moment of reading through this book series. Borrowing from Vasco’s ideas this can be a great topic for the study group or even an open university!

Toby and Vasko, I shall try to pickup some of the patterns you have mentioned.
I shall take a bit of liberty to bring in new patterns that I think will interact in the given scenario. Here I am again bringing my own terminology-apologies and I shall first state my conventions : Any real life solution/situation I refer to as scene. My idea is such a solution will always emerge as an interaction between multiple patterns. Some of these patterns will be interrelated through a hierarchy while others will be quite independent of one another. Also same patterns may be related differently in different scenes. Focus is the cross between a pattern and a scene.
The numbering scheme is not achieving any thing except they show how a solution can be found through interaction and drilling through several patterns from more general to less general one until they come down to a focus that delivers a solution. So the numbering scheme will change depending on the scene considered. For my convenience I shall take my house as the current scene –just because I am more familiar with the scene. So the purpose of this exercise is to see whether this sort of scheme is acceptable or appealing to you-whether or not you think it will help to get to a solution.. This is directly derived from the current model I have of patterns and its software counterpart. .
Some of the patterns interacting at my house scene are:: Maintaining Life at every corner of the house” - a general pattern that will have a pattern "Life Style in South facing Houses" as a sub-pattern. Where as "Community Interaction with a house" is another pattern which is interacting with the first one but they are not directly linked through any hierarchy.

This exercise will give us certain kind of focus that will be useful, amongst other things to see how ultimately different sections of the community can interact to bring up a solution. Mostly I am interested in the representation of patterns so that they can be part of normal business transactions. Also it gives some idea about the complexity of interaction of social structures like lawyers, councils and governments that is required.

Coming to the numbering I have got a few patterns to start: Mostly they are scattered but related-we need far more patterns to derive any solution. All the patterns listed are type 'S': they are not implementation related. [I shall have very little knowledge on the implementation front]. Some of you can extend this hierarchy as you get more ideas for implementation or otherwise.
The highest patterns are:
1. Maintaining Life at Every Corner of the house.
2. Community Interaction with the house.
3. Using geographic topology to bring harmony in house
4. Lively old buildings in the country [from Georgina's description of country potentials, not necessarily applicable for my house]
Sub-patterns for pattern 1: . Maintaining Life at Every Corner of the house
1.1 Arrangement of living room with respect to other rooms
1.2 Arrangement of Kitchen with respect to other rooms
1.3 Dealing with Dampness and lack of sunshine in the rooms
1.3.1 Fireplaces to remove damp
1.3.2 Air duct to increase inside air flow
1.3.3 Sun light through tunnels
1.4 Life Style in South facing Houses
1.5 Overall solar aspect in a house
Sub-patterns for pattern 2 . Community Interaction with the house
2.1 Front of House and street life continuity
2.1.1 Home front for the kids
2.1.2 Courtyards which live
2.1.3 Half-private gardens
2.2 Community interaction within home
2.2.1 Owner builder brings culture and traditional life
2.3 Council's role in community interaction
2.3 Back-yard Entertainment for guests
2.4 Front-yard Entertainment for guests
Sub-patterns for pattern 3 Using geographic topology to bring harmony in house
3.1 House on a slope
3.1.1 Retaining walls with the front access stairs
3.1.2 Retaining walls at the backyard garden.
3.2 Using slope to your advantage
3.2.1 Using water flow down the slope to clean swimming pool water
3.2.2 Water flow to drive fan in the air-duct
4. Lively Old Buildings in the Country
4.1 Cheaper but livelier houses
Your suggestions and criticism welcome.
Speak to you soon

Georgina Chaseling 23:03:32 4/10/2002
Hi All,
There has been lots of talking while I concentrating in another wave of activity on my building.
In answer to your question Vasko, I bought an old Mechanics Institute building in Boorowa last year. It has three sections, the first the hall and two side libraries and two rooms at the back of the hall, were built in 1883. The supper room constructed about 1910, which runs the full width of the hall at the back, and in 1930s, following its purchase by the CWA for the cost of the debts of the Mechanics Institute organisation, the kitchen and baby health centre was built on the back again, to the north. The back section is where I am living. The front and older section is in better condition than the rear, partly as the hall was built on massive rubble stone foundations and the new section was built in the depression with the accompanying cost cutting measures like no grip in the mortar.
It is interesting that more people who are interested in a non city life style do not come out to established country towns and snap up some of the marvelous buildings which are quietly falling to pieces and being demolished. All the materials are there, in our town at least, competent tradesmen, and the cost is small. I paid $75,000 for a 50 sq building in full brick on an acre of land with all services.
This might help in establishing the 'bottom up' grass roots level of change and perhaps be better than communities which "lock themeselves away" so to speak in more isolated communities. I am not knocking those communities, but I think there are some additional approaches.
I also have a community vegetable patch ready to go, and the reading rooms and library will be complemented by the bookshop, which hopefully will be able to sell local produce and products.
I could also host the conference on integration of patterns, and show people what country town living can offer. Mind you the town is not perfect! and council discussion is better left to a more secure email. I agree about the building of more unusual structures, they might get more acceptance if they are built in country town areas first, and establish their credibility, in mainstream building practices.
Georgina Chaseling

Georgina Chaseling From Boorowa, Australia

vasko drogriski 20:23:20 4/06/2002
Hi Tobby,

Yes l agree, owner building can make you poor, atleast in the immediate future. But like a plant storing sunlight and nutrient for its future growth, you have probably gained and stored much intellectual capital that'll serve you and others well at different times in life from now.

l can understand what you are saying about beauracrats. l have also had some experience with them. l have found that often they take either of two positions, the path of least resistance, that you have mentioned, which often means giving you most resistance, particularly when you suggest something a little out of the ordinary. The other position they can take is where they put the onus on you to proove and substantiate your proposal, while they completely remove themselves from any responsibility or accountability. We often found this while working as eco-designers in Melbourne, building with earth brick and strawbales for example.
The building surveyors and other council beauracrats often took either of these two positions, maximum resistance or no resistance at all.
Both these positions have l believe one underlying agenda, or driving cause in common, that is the legal realms of litigation, ie; protecting oneself from litigation.
So, for council surveyors, engineers, beauracrats, their position is to try to make any innovation very difficult (simply because as you would know, innovation is experimentation, and experimentation can lead to failure or unexpected results) and if you can not do that then you absolve yourself from any responsibility and put all the responsibilty on the other, ie; often owner builders in the case of building.
If we kept talking about the whole dynamics here of litigation, responsiblity, public liability, protection of property, we would soon come to the insurance companies. This is where l believe much of what we are talking about has it's wellspring.
And beyond the wellspring, is the larger 'aquifer' which contains other things which also deserve attention. But most of us are probably in agreement that much of what is in this underlying 'aquifer' is many of the things we instinctively feel are things about Capitalism.

We can keep this in mind. At the immediate moment however, l would like to hear more about your experiences in owner building. What was good about it, what was not so good, what patterns were useful, what weren't etc...
After building load bearing mudbrick, my partners and l, half jokingly and half seriously, decided to form a 'mudbrick workers liberation army'. Extremely labour intensive, as is strawbale building. We think that building with these materials is a lot more difficult than the fringe movements make out.
We also decided that building with these materials is more appropriate for cummunities who build together, and not so suitable for example for an isolated nuclear family building itself a house in the city. We feel this is even more so for strawbales. This is not to say that people should not use these materials.

What is your feeling about mudbrick building?

As for energy efficiency, l agree that the Energy rating programs are not very good.
But l am also not convinced yet about any claims of the need for sophisticated simulations and measurment of 'energy efficiency'.
These measurments can never deal with the subjective and human patterns of movement through buildings.
Why can't we instead work on our metabolism and biorythms to tune in to the weather better, as Georgina has pointed out?

l think the discussion with HT Odum would be extremely valuable, as also with permaculture and David Holmegren.
We can get good cross fertilization between and across disciplines if we did this, particularly if we joined other discussions which are more specifically relating social justice and community issues. These are often central to discussions of ecological justice, and in fact, they are really two sides of the same coin. Any culture which has not become so detached from nature, such as ours, would know this as a matter of coarse.

Talk to you again.

vasko drogriski From Melbourne, Australia

Toby Channing 21:25:56 4/02/2002
Dear Vasco, Pronob and others...
Great discussion, unfortunatly i've been off line for a while due to owner-builder induced poverty!
Reading through the previous mails has inspired me to make the following dubious claims...

To further the discussion re: why have some organisations dominated the buiding feild with their specific views?
I belive that beaurocrates will usually follow the path of least resistance, whilst guarding against whatever threatens their power. For example a Shire Engineer can do calculations on a required bridge, or use a premade propritety product that comes supplied with engineering comps and a garentee, you pick the path of least resistance! The threat to the engineer is the bridge failing. The product is garenteed, so the threat is dealt with. However this standardisation results in loss of flexability is design options, the engineers skill in designing for the local environment, and usuially a massive over use of materials.
Neither do most of us challenge publications because we were tought at school that truth come in book.
When the only truth come is a book we lose our oral traditions, why trust locals builders experiance when you can consult AS1684.4? Orally I have learned that old houses (perhaps Pronobs damp house in Sydney?) stayed dry by the ventilation caused by fires burning all year (cooking etc...) drawing a constant supply of air through the house. This is not in AS1684.4!
The beauty of the Pattern Language is that the generalsiations are general, ie every house built will interact with the sun. Patterns that are more climate appropriate are used in 'clumps' of patterns, or ignored. This is permaculture, it cannot be acheived prescritive legislation, or the NATHERS five star program. My passive solar mud brick house that has been mathmatically designed to require no suplementry heating does not rate as well as superinsulated box, that is electrcally heated. One of the foundations of permaculture is H.T.Odums general systems theory of ecology that attemps to compare apples with apples by relating all enery to its original sunlight value. Sound like i'm getting off track but bear with me. If my house
where heated with 10 mega joules of wood per year, the five star ideology would not differentiate between 10 mega joules of electrical energy. If both were expressed in their sunlight equivalents a massive difference becomes apparent. Think of the free work of nature. Wood; sunlight-clorofil-carbon storage-suger creation-wood. (this is all from memory so please don't quote!)Electricity; sunlight-clorofil-sugars-biomass-massive geological energy imputs-coal-large scale mining-burning (35% eff.)transmition (50% eff.). So the higher the energy quality the higher the initial energy quantity. Therefore 10 mega joules of wood energy takes the planet substancially less energy to create than 10 mega joules of electricall energy. There! you never thought you'd say low quality is good!
Back to the simplicity of patterns to control growth well. The Incan hill top cities were built with every building getting full solar acess, no building overshadows any other. Simple patterns with powerfull results.
Bill molisons permaculte book is a great read, but hard to apply. more recent publications from David Holmgren,and others are more refined.
Capitalism. I used to get really cross. More recently however I have been having some other thoughts. What if all political systems where languges. Languages that change when differednt patterns become, or cease to be, supportable. Perhaps capitalsim is a language of growth, or resource (read energy) dispersal. We have dispersed, in the last 100 years, an energy concentration that took the planet 400 million years to capture, concentrate and store from sunlight.
I've drawn a bit of a long bow with a few of these ideas, but I hope you have found them to be relevent to the exploration of pattern understanding.

Love you all!!!

Hi guys,
Apologies for the delayed response. Been under the weather lately.

Georgina, capitalism has hijacked our world. It's also true that capitalism has spoiled the environment, starved 2/3 of the people on the planet, and for those of us who are not starving we are instead dying of boredom. It really isn't that good for us. l can see your point.
And l also agree that things should only and can only be changed from the bottom. l believe that patterns can contribute to the bottom up changing of the world.
But l also believe that it is possible for ideas like patterns to be co-opted or "commodified" and used to benefit those who have the time and leisure and means to make themselves the most beatiful surroundings, for themselves only, and put large walls and gates around themselves.
What of our past, and our ancestors, is useful to us? l suppose it varies from person to person and from culture to culture. But for me, l guess the sense of belonging and community is what l feel is the greatest loss from our past and ancestors that we don't have in modern society.
The internet can help to make new forms of communities but l'm not hopefull that the internet will be the saviour either, not alone anyway.
My most pessimistic response is that we won't balance capitalisms bad patterns with good patterns (because capitalism is more efficient at destroying than we are at building).
My most optimistic response to capitalism is that we will eternally live in boredom and mental illness if we did find a balance in it.
Georgina, l think that the issue you raise is a difficult one for patterns.
l suppose we just have to see what the "Nature of Order" says on Capitalism, history and the future.
In any case, l am keen to keep up this line of discussion.

But l also agree with Pronob about staying focused.
And Pronob, here is another pattern for us to apply some numbering to. This is a pattern l have adapted from a Pattern language. It is "Half private garden" which l use in conjunction with "Minimum offset for houses from the street". This pattern is one that l have had some dramas with at councils with council town planners.
As council enforce the minimum offset from the street, l use the "Half private garden" at the front to make this zone useful. Usually the minimum offset rule leads to baron lawnscapes or de-facto car parks or car cemeteries in front of peoples houses. In most cases, the result is non living front yards. In a sense, space that has neither any public virtue or quality, nor any private use. Its like the Bermuda Triangle for automobiles.
The "half private garden" rescues this space l believe. It gives a good transition zone from the house to the street as well as allowing the household to interact with the street life and community in general. "Courtyards which live" can also be used in the same way.
But council have a problem with this, and l think it is largely cultural bias. They think that spaces can either be private or public. Half private is just a bit wierd. Why would you want to have something that is half private? What is half private? Is it private or not private? they ask.
And besides, if it is meant to be private, then they can not count it in the overall requirements of provision of private open space for dwellings. So, l have kept working away at different councils. l have found ways of getting some to accept the validity of such a pattern.
But this pattern is useful in another sense. It allows a designer, on most sites, to have both at least private north facing living areas and otional south facing living areas, which l would argue are important for our climate. This is important also from the point that most subdivisions are not ideally oriented for good solar aspect. In other words it extends the design possibilities by broadening the context and design response parameters, if this makes sense.
Pronob, how would you go about recording or numbering here? Please comment.

Talk to you both again.

Georgina Chaseling 19:19:32 3/23/2002
Hi Vasko, Pronob, et al,
My opinion of building codes, engineering, materials etc is that, along with lots of others things in our world, housing has been hijacked by capitalism. It seems that the only way to make a change, by 'patterns' or anything else, is to make changes ourselves, and spread the 'pattern' from the bottom up. Things to include would be choice of where we live, climate, aspect, location; and how we live, in concrete boxes which are economical to build and realise maximum return for the builder, or in human- friendly places where we can reach our full potential as people.
My thought is that the further we get from our ancestors, in our style of living the less happy we will be.
For example, I think we need contact with the seasons, with changing weather, even proper divisions between night and day. We need open spaces, and things that are green, and fresh water. One of our problems is that technology has moved too fast, and the brain has not had enough time, like probably thousands of years, to accommodate change.
Perhaps it is enough to return some 'ancient' things to our modern lives. Sunny rooms, climate variation, fresh grown food, while still keeping the commodities of society. Is it a matter of balancing patterns of society, of building, of commodification, of accepting some and modifying or rejecting others.
What do you think?
Georgina

It will be good if we can distinguish the pattern arising from such subjective issues from patterns created in terms of physical features,constrain and practises like 'minimum width of the front yard' or the height of the chimney etc. It is understandable such physical characterstics will be the cause and constrains of other physical features like 'minimum area of the plot for a apartment block' etc; so conceivably such physical characterstics and their dependencies will very much emerge as some patterns-I suspect these will have lots of technical jargons and engineering guidelines and principles . But it will be worth while if from the begining we keep such patterns arising from physical constrains as seperate from more subjective patterns which a layman can relate to . We can follow a convention where the last dot is followed by S[subjective] or a P[physical/practising].Eg the pattern "front set back for houses' can become 1.S, where as a pattern like 'measurements for an apartment block' can be given a number 2.P etc; it is quite possible that a subjective patterns will spawn or refer to a more physical/practising pattern and vice versa. Good evening Pronob,

North facing areas would definitely help with the damp problem, and so will good cross ventilation.
l might have mentioned earlier that l reckon l have a pattern to compliment north facing areas, and that is shady areas on the south. This can also be a flywire enclosed room on the south, with ferns and stones and water. It can be used to cool your home in summer. The sunny areas on the north can have high windows which open from the bottom downwards and the shady south edge of the house can have low windows which open from the top and outwards into the shady room.
l think passive cooling in our climate is possible. l have not seen its full potential developed in any particular areas in Australia. It seems to me that for Australias climate, it would have had just as much attention as passive heating has had in energy efficient architecture.
So south facing rooms are not necessarily a bad thing in a Cool Temperate climate like Melbourne, and probably much of Sydney, although l think Sydney is a bit more humid isn't it?
As you point out though, your place has the south facing areas but not the north facing ones. Maybe you can use some skylights or skytubes to get some sunlight from the north and east sky into the south parts of the building.

vasko drogriski 17:16:30 3/09/2002
Hello Toby,

Hey its cool, the site belongs to us all. I'm glad you've visited us.

l totally agree that the large timber/forestry, concrete and engineering bodies have absolutely dominated building culture, they have heavily influenced building codes and design, (not to mention what insurance companies have done also). The building codes and the 'design patterns' imposed by these large private and public bodies have totally colonised the patterns which traditionally were used collectively by our communities.
But in the first place they have succeeded in doing this by destroying communities, (and an example in building is how the rights of the owner builder has been eroded over the decades since the 50's, this offensive is continued now against the owner builder by the banks for example).

Apoligies for the rant, you're right, we can cut the crap if we got straight to permaculture.

Without belitlleing your efforts out at Fryers Forest, (l appreciate the difficulties you must have had trying to form a community out there with radical ideas for living ecologically and collectively, l hate to think what your council was like) but my difficulty is that l have to work day in and day out with these building codes and design guidelines. l am on a daily basis having to contend with them, dissect them to find their merit and challenge them with better patterns like permaculture and Christopher Alexanders patterns.

To pick up a specific point of yours that "Bad patterns can be made existant simply by published biased data, rather than relying on the knowledge that our cultures contain",
It's absolutely right what you're saying. That's all it takes really. And the published word then becomes gospel.
But why? Why does the published biased data have such persistance and ability to permeate into peoples consciousness, especially when it's not true?

There is an ecological pattern that is at present under threat (amongst all the rest that are under threat). It is the pattern of "North facing outdoors" or, "Living areas to the north".
Henley Homes, which is a large Building company in Melbourne, now claim that they can build a five star energy rated home. This five star home is a response by Henley to Legislation which soon may be introduced in Victoria for all new homes to have a minimum of 4 stars.
Well, when l heard, l thought, that's good, the big players are forced to respond in a responsible way in these times of impending ecological disaster. l later found out however that Henley can get five star ratings simply by enveloping their houses in very high insulation, icluding aluminium throughout the walls while they even faced their houses west or even south.
Tricky buggers aren't they. They've used bad patterns to replace good patterns. And the clients are happy cause they have an environmentally friendly home.
When l first bagan designing homes to face the sun, my clients, who were mostly from southern european climates, were really not that keen. They wanted me to design shady areas on the south for them. Melbourne's winter was mild for them but Melbourne's summer was unbearable, particularly the sun, as they were accustomed to much colder winters and milder summers.
So these clients, who are often the same clients that Henley now build homes for, don't mind that their homes are facing south, but they do like the fact that their home is going to use less energy and be cheaper to run.
What is not often in the equation though is how healthy these homes are either, but people are cottoning on to this also now, as most of these southern european people are dying of cancer and they can't drink red wine cause the doctor has given them tablets to drink instead, often for diabetes and blood pressure. Increasingly they're asking how come so many of us are taking tablets.
There's a joke going around in the Macedonian community, one friend says to another;
Would you like a drink?
No, l'm on talblets!
Anyway, that aside, it would be good to visit Fryers forest sometime, l have visited a couple of times, but many years ago. Might see you there sometime.

Speak to you again.

vasko drogriski From Melbourne, Australia

l have been trying to collect my thoughts about patterns and building codes over the last couple of days.
There are a number of angles from which to approach the subject, all equally complex and difficult.
l am most interested in the social and cultural aspects of our building codes and design guidelines. That is, how do building codes reflect the culture and social setup that we live in, and how do they help in turn to support that structure which gives rise to them.
In this sense codes and guidelines are a type of patterns for the society that we live in, except that most of them are bad patterns.
l am interested in where these bad patterns come from. On the other hand l am also interested in where the good patterns come from.
For example there is a building code and design guideline in the new Residential Code of Victoria which says that, for new houses or multiple houses on a site the set back of the new house from the frontage should be the average of the two houses on either side of it or 9m, whichever is the lesser. This is l believe a sort of pattern. It gives a context and a solution. How did this guideline come into being?
Because in a neighbourhood where front setbacks are uniform and frontyards are baron lawnscapes, or parking lots, that is, dead spaces, what is the real meaning of this guideline? In other words, does this guideline have cultural roots or purely technical and engineering origins concerned with infrastructure.

The other side of building codes and design guidelines is the technical side. The side that engineers, surveyors, councils and town planners are involved in.
What is the role of these professionals in the rules, apart from administering and enforcing the rules. Also, what is there background and interpretation of guidelines.

The other side is the professinals like myself who use the rules to design the built environment for others to live in.

l suppose the subject is even more complex when we realise that there are connections between the social, cultural, technical and administrative sides in their effect on how building codes and design guidelines take their shape.

History keeps coming to my mind throughout all of these subjects.
When did this or that code come into place for example, why did it come into place, what were the particular historical context for its emergence?

So Pronob, l will ask for your feedback at this stage. Are any of these issues of particular interest to you for discussion?

Pronob Pal 21:36:39 3/03/2002
Good Day Vasko,

Yes, you are right about how end user requirement drives software reuse and maintenance, but the point I was making about design re-use is more fundamental in the way we design software solutions. In the traditional way of software development ,the software maker gets the software working and then writes a user manual -which instructs the potential users about how to do specific things like [in case of the word-processor] copying a phrase ,pasting at the end of the paragraph etc .
But effectively there is a much more complex transaction going on in the background.
What the software maker is doing is slowly bringing the user to the world [in terms of software] he/she has designed.
I suppose the same thing happens in any other kind of design. For example the automobile design -the way the gear ,clutch, accelerator combination work is part of the design of the car-it is just that it has become such a widely accepted standard that it has become a pattern-taken-for granted.
However in a software package the functions required and their associated techniques are so numerous that it is
not possible to work around any such established pattern. Other fact is of course the software packages are also being constantly invented and constantly evolving.
We can say by learning to use a software package the user is introduced to the world designed by the
software maker.I am describing reuse of design from this perspective-reused by the user. As the user becomes more and more expert in the package
the user gets more and more inside the world designed by the software designer.


You can see this more vividly in the real world when the university graduates become the executives in the
commercial world they choose the package [-be that be operating system or the database-] that is more familiar to them.
No wonder the software companies are willing to make generous contributions to the education institutions in terms of software and hardware.
It is quite possible to design a software package that does lots of things. But how can you pre-define everything? It is not a healthy practice to try to design every thing for the user. It is far better practice to design something so the user requirement can evolve while the user lives a his/ her normal life. Assuming this is good practice ,it is far better if the user requirement can be allowed to evolve in a world
which drives the user rather than through the software package someone designed to do some specific task.
This is what pattern based software design and content based computing is focussing on.
For example a mechanical designer should be able to specify and evolve with his/ her requirement in the mechanical design world.For example he might say "..,now that I can
draw the train track and the train, I want to show the amount of friction that is generated as the train moves faster..."


On the question of why the code does not contain the design- you might guess this has been a problem through out our computing history.
We have tried to fix it through elaborate documentation or even smart tools /packages. The fact is documentation in isolation of the code and the object code [generated from the
code] become useless for two reasons. Documentation in isolation cannot establish the right context for execution of the code and
also the code can be changed easily without changing the documentation at all [in real life this happens very often]. Content based computing is built on the premise that computation progresses in the same fashion that a human being understands the system. This ensures the code is a replica of a content that human being
understands in the specific context. You are right on the point in suggesting .....content based computing can store design knowledge of the architecture
or the particular structures..
Of course this kind of solution brings in other issues like intellectual property , security rights and also performance issues to the front.Each of these issues is a seperate dimension to the software design challenge. The solution to these issues is not to design something half or restrict the dimensions of growth but to allow it to grow full in all the dimensions.
Traditional computing is based on the Van-Neuman model where input- process -output defines the scope and result of computation. In contrast, pattern-based computing pattern tour determines the context. The pattern tour provides a path similar to human understanding
while the interaction of different patterns within a scene provides the dynamics of computation.

Why Microsoft is not doing it? There is certainly business interest to build new ones which can be built only as the extension of the old ones - however,I do not believe that is the only reason why things like pattern based computing has not found its root in the academic and commercial world.

One reason is not enough people know about it. The other reason, the architects of the new industry is too busy fighting the old fires. I sent some write up to a person quite well known in the computing world who had also his interest in Patterns. By the way, interest in Patterns has been with software community for the last 10-12 years.
But he has returned my writing to me saying he is too busy with his other projects to pass any judgment on something that is deep enough to propose a new way of computing.
Pattern based computing, if it can take root in the mainstream computing will not only benefit the software community but it shall provide a kind of meta-grammer on which other professional and
literary disciplines can build their own patterns and transact through patterns.
That is all for now. I hope I have not dampened your interest in Pattern based computing by suggesting this is something foreign to the mainstream software world.

This morning I had a look at the Rosneath web-site -no doubt very commendable effort to build communities
on eco-village environment.Hopefully they will teach us ,the rest of the world about new approaches to manage
the environments and design houses and community facilities. I am including the site address for others who might be interested.:www.rosneath.com.au
Thanks


Pronob Pal From Sydney, Australia

Pronob Pal 20:22:45 2/28/2002
Hello Vasko,
Firstly reuse and maintenance of software design is in the nature of the current software technology and how it fits into our normal life. Any piece of software of course have some requirement to start with. But
very often we find that as soon as we have developed the software the requirement changes or
we get additional requirements.
You may not realize it with a common piece of software like the
word-processor -that is because
the way we are tied up with the distribution and marketing of it.Just to
give an example ,suppose you need a word processor to give to your grandmother who will like to use it
to write periodic simple letters and poetry for her grand-children.To start she was interested in writing words-she wont need
'online collaboration' or 'auto summary' or 'thesaurus'-and other numerous features that come with the word processor -
slowly she became interested not only in writing words but also in painting pictures -the software should have unfolded
such things quite naturally bringing in features as she wanted, For this to happen, she would not have to show special smartness
towards the computer tasks -she should have picked the necessary skills as easily as she writes two rhyming sentences.
But this does not happen in real life. One is considered to be extra-smart just because one is able to use a package what Microsoft has developed
after spending billions in usability testing labs. This can be interpreted as a reuse of design-where the product design is supposed to unfold to the end-user easily. But of course with the current sate of affairs that does not happen.The design reuse that is called for here is a quality in the overall design of the whole word processor so that the design of little pieces [like drawing pictures] becomes apparent
to the user of those pieces easily just by coming to the specific context.Thus in the example when grand mother
is ready to draw pictures she commands draw picture when the word processor
knows a topical line in the letter and brings drawing matching the topic or suggests related topics through matching with patterns matching rest of the content 'keywords' in the letter.

There is another design reuse-related to maintenance-the situation is frequent in a commercial world ,where to change a designed software
which e.g. does some smart calculation to measure the performance of bank employees, one has to know the business rules that prompted the design
and its associated calculations -but the person who had done that originally had gone somewhere else taking with him the ability of the software
to evolve with the changing business world for the bank. The new person assigned to do the design changes takes longer time in changing the design. Because the code of the software does not hold the design knowledge, it is quite easy for the new person to exceed the original
design effort in an effort to find out and reuse the original design to bring in the desired changes.
I believe the solution of these problems can be built into the software architecture by building a new model of computation based in pattern-based computing.

Having said this much I am also interested in hearing from other members in patternlanguage.com who
might have computing background-this is specially because if I have to talk about specific role of patterns as I see, it would be a biased view towards my own way of representation of patterns. We shall speak about that in due course.Thanks

Pronob Pal From Sydney, Australia

Pronob Pal 23:19:48 2/26/2002
Vasko,
My interest in Patterns is from the point of view of reuse of design. However, at the same time I am interested in giving patterns some kind of expression that shall help us better maintain or reuse an existing design. I am not sure how much
of this design reuse or maintenance aspect come into play in Architecture but it is certainly a major issue in the software field where in general software maintenance cost more than software design and development.
Starting from the example you provided:the pattern of timber,slate and concrete floor, first thing I shall
suggest that this is not a pattern, but an application of a pattern. After looking at this example,some one can do a floor sketch for a library room with book shelves along the four walls and some display item in the middle. The wooden part of the floor is layed parallel to the four walls,idea is people,without shoes, will stand mostly next to the book shelves when they are in this room.The library room still implements the pattern that you suggested. But what can be the description of the pattern you suggested? Before I put my suggestion about that, I like to draw your attention to the fact that I have got my own definition of patterns which I have also used in my site papers and other softwares. In my model, pattern is nothing but a consequtive sequence of the focus of the mind. A collection of several related focus is called a Scene. In reality a Scene can be a free flowing description of the solution as you presented. A description like that in general has several patterns flowing through it.
Coming back to the example you provided, I can suggest several patterns[my brand of patterns] flowing through it.
e.g "Comfortable Floors For Solar House" is one, others can be "Maintaining thermal mass in a solar House", "location of Solar rooms in temperate climate" etc.
My point is all these patterns exist simultaneously in your particular example.It may appear that these descriptions of patterns are focussing on the problem rather than the solution like a more accepted version of pattern does. But I have no problem with that -I can easily call the patterns like "Floor with , timber, concrete ", "Wooden Floor for thermal retention" ,"North Face for Solar room" etc.
My point is, it is essential to give Patterns a "standard 'normalised' form" with simplicity of concept.
If we accept the above approach, the pattern "Comfortable Floors For Solar House" can be thought of as a narrative with consequtive sections on various aspects of the title of the pattern. For example there can be section on the comfort aspect of the floor, concentrating on relation between floor material and blood flow through the feet. There can be a section on materials possible for floors. Point to note none of these sections will have only the single pattern in question. Each section will have other numerous patterns flowing through it just like your example does. What I am saying is,
Patterns can be compared with strings of multilayered beads hanging together from the neck. A pattern can be thought of as a string going through large beads where each bead has a number of thread penetrable wholes. Each string passes throgh some selective beads but all together the beads hang from the neck of the wearer as if stuck on a single wide band around the neck.
Vasko, if you are happy with this simplification of patterns I can go on discussing other aspects of patterns -of how we can use them through
software tools to aid in architecture work in dynamic design environment [patterns are not static design aspect any more,they would define the action at almost every little design step]. Here I shall wait for your thought before I proceed further.
Thanks

Pronob Pal From Sydney, Australia

http://www.visualanalytics.com.au

vasko drogriski 04:42:28 2/25/2002
Pronob.

Thanks for your site. l did read your papers.
How did you get interested in patterns first?
How do we get a database to collect patterns and stories related to their places?

l am interested in your comment about patterns being not only documents of good practice but drivers of design.

How do patterns become validated?

For example, l think l have discovered, or rediscovered some patterns in my work.
They are:

Seasonal pond
Flywire enclosure
Shady area on the south
and l have a pattern for a timber, slate and concrete floor.
These three materials can be combined together to make a floor that looks beautiful and gives you good thermal mass.
You can make a floor like this for a passive solar house, it is probably best to make this floor in the north facing rooms that get best sunlight. In the past passive solar buildings used concrete slabs to get thermal mass for the building for both winter heat storage and also for summer heat absorption, thereby having a moderating effect on the internal temperatures.
But concrete slabs can also be cold in winter and hard and not very comfortable to walk on.
So l drew a sketch of a floor that had a band of polished cocrete around the room, roughly about 600mm wide, sometimes it can be a metre, depending on the size of the room. Then you have a row of green slate tiles inside this, about 250mm for their width, and within the green slate tiles you have a recycled redgum or jarrah floor recessed into the slab and flush with the tiles or concrete.
This way you get the best of all worlds. You get the thermal mass that for your building and where you sit mostly, you have a timber floor that is warmer and easier on your feet than concrete.
l made this pattern after l built my first loadbearing mudbrick house. This is when l realised how difficult it was building with mudbridks.

l am trying to make these patterns for a cool temperate climate like here in Melbourne.

vasko drogriski From Melbourne, Australia

Pronob Pal 05:34:09 2/23/2002
Vasko,
Thanks for your last two responses.
I shall start with a brief background where I am coming from. Although my interest in Patterns has been through my interest in Software Architecture, it is something else which attracted me to Software Architecture in the first place.
That something else includes an knack towards observation of the process of human understanding [if there is any process at all].
In this domain I believe patterns have a major role to play. After carefull consideration of what goes on in different computational activity, I strongly believe the only
way we can take leverage of this ever-present 'Patterns' is by building all our computational tools like software programs on a different kind of computational platform which I called Content based computing. If you have a spare time you are most welcome to read a paper I wrote on this -it is in my site-the address of which appears below.

Your narration of a practicing architect's encounter with Patterns and other human beings has to some extent supports my belief about Patterns. Patterns,I believe can be and should be
made part of the language between the architects and as well as between the architects and their clients.
Expression of patterns has to be something which we understand just by knowing english -one need not be trained in any particular discipline to understand patterns. For example "going to school" can be a pattern. Also patterns can be nested e.g. 'going to school' can have another pattern built into :'catching the transport'.This may sound like I am trivialising patterns by ignoring such pre-requisites like context,problem,forces of nature etc.
But we need some formal framework to represent every pattern in a way that patterns are just not documentation of good practices but patterns become the drivers of design in the tool sense as well. However that does not mean patterns loose their subjective gravity. All it means is patterns become the vehicle of transactions between people in the society, between professionals.

Coming back to the architect's service ,imagine we have a standard convention where we describe a structure by a short expression of the very human activity that goes on
in and around that structure. Imagine there is a world-wide standards data base of such expressions-something similar to domain names for internet addresses. Against the short description,in this case, the data base has some graphical description of the pattern of that structure it is referring to.

For example we can describe two garden styles:
one is "Indian Puja Garden" and the other is "Japanese Tea".
Now these two structure for gardens expresses certain combination of facilities ,like a group of people to
do some ceremony or practice, the first being where a group of 10-15 people sit together on aplatform and a priest sit on an elevated level.
The tea garden is more for a group of 5 couples where each couple has a separate place to sit.
Both those styles of garden might include [nested] a pattern like "free-flowing fresh air". With easy access and representation of such patterns and their graphical views , Patterns will become more part of the transactions not only between architects but also between architects and clients. Without my background in architecture these examples are quite superficially made up. But I suppose you can get the idea of what sort of role for patterns I am thinking of. It may appear this is a long way from the state today-but in the internet age no one really knows the speed of rush to the future.

Pronob Pal From Sydney, Australia

http://www.visualanalytics.com.au

vasko drogriski 17:43:41 2/22/2002
Pronob,

l would like to try and answer your last question from your most recent entry;
How can patterns help improve architec services?
l am trying to answer this for my own sake, because l am also trying to understand the answer to the question.
l work for a private architecture firm and have been trying to introduce the patterns into the services of our firm.
So far l have had more luck with the clients than with the directors.
In my mind your question has two parts to it, at least.
The first part can be answered directly to the question, and this is much easier for me to answer.
Patterns can help architect services in many ways. One of the most important ways they can help is that they provide a common language between the architect and client, as well as to any other people involved in a particular building project like the builders and tradespeople.
Patterns can help the architect specifically by unravelling to the architect the organic nature between built structures and the way humans inhabit space and time in their myriad of actions from the most mundane to the most profound.
Patterns in this sense give human actions quite a primary role as determining influences in the way buildings and human habitations take their shape.
Today however, architects begin design the other way around. They start with a 'bright' idea, often this is a form, a shape, a geometry of some sort, then they squeeze the living actions of people into the those particular spaces.
According to patterns this is just not the way things happen, they have never happened this way for humans in the past.
The other side of your question for me is why have patterns not been embraced or used more widely by architects and other design and building professionals?
l have only known about patterns for a short time myself.
l handed one of the patterns books to my director who is in his 50's and was around at the time when patterns were emerging in the USA. He had not heard of patterns but was quite enthuasiastic and inquisitive about them and wanted to have a look.
He flicked through the pages , and have you ever seen someone throw a dog a handfull of rabbits guts, how it lunges eagerly at them initially, and then realising after having half swallowed a mouthfull, that it does not really like the taste, then recoils and backs away, growling and convulsing as it shakes the contents right back out. Well this is what my director was like. And like the tempted and curious dog,skirting around afterwards and nipping at and licking at the what it had just expelled, so too my director skirted around the book and ate one page here and one page there, but not the whole lot.
l suppose it had that raw, human, fleshy taste to him. Too strong. He later described it as too 'deep'.
l am still trying to still understand what he did not like about the patterns.
Our firm is a medium sized firm, with building consultants and architects and surveyors all working together. Most of the blokes, particularly the directors are suspicious of most things, particularly these pattern things.
The women on the other hand, who are mostly in secreterial and admin. roles think that it's all fine and in fact quite important.
The clients who l have been giving the patterns to, want patterns with cream on top.
And then there are the cleaners who come in at the end of every day to clean our crap and cups and food everywhere. They hardly speak a word of english but understand these patterns. They reckon that;
"Yeah, ofcoarse you have to plant fruit trees and vegetables in your backyard, these patterns of yours are nothing new, we know them already, our parents have been doing it like that for a long time you know".
So now my clients are asking for more patterns, and the directors are seeing these clients eating these 'rabbits guts' and their eyes bulge and water and their cheeks puff up and glow... cause its all a bit hard for them.
l keep telling them we can improve our services with these patterns. And they're not that stupid that they can't see cause they really are quite canny and shrewd.
My best understanding of why they don't like the patterns at the moment is based on superficial appearances of their behaviour. They're trying to work out if these patterns are going to be a staple diet in the future, and should they start learning how to eat them?

vasko drogriski From Melbourne, Australia
