Pronob Pal 06:50:03 2/20/2002
Reading the comments so far I guess every one has been interested in pattern from aechitecture-related perspective. My experience with arcitecture has been as an user of services from architects, and that too is not terribly positive one-I spent around $10,000 on some architectural plans for the renovation of the house I live in. The architects produced about 5 sketches starting from initial sketch to developed plans and because I had to postpone the project because of personal circumstances I just ended up paying the prorata on the completed task, the total architecture cost being 9% of the estimated budget of the project. This may have been far more interactive and suggestive phase of the potential of the place I live in, had the architects approached the issue from a different perspective. To start,they might have suggested a few alternate ways I can set up my back yard.Like how it can add value not only to my property but also adds some attraction to the neighbourhood.They could have made some alternative sketches about the way we can use our swimming pool-not only just for swimming but also as a calming agent for us and our tenanats who live next door-or how we can have alternative entertainment area for sitting under the tree or next to swimming pool etc.Instead the architects interest was totally focussed on two things-one is our buget and the other was what we ourselves want. The fact is budget is to some extent related to the potential of the building structure and ourselves, not being architects, not necessarily know what is possible given the position of our land and neighbourhood.
This is where patterns may come handy-if the architects were follower of patterns it would have been quite possible for them to give us some possible alternatives without charging $10,000. I guess same thing is happening at other places as well where people are building some thing because that would presumably fetch highest financial return or it is the cheapest to build. In this rush other issues and mental preferences does not get much chance to play.
I am a software pwerson by profession. I can probably imagine systems holding information on patterns -but will like to hear the point of view of practising architects -how do you think pattern can enhance the architecture service in general? Can it be used to protray a possible lifestyle the future structure will help to bring in?

Pronob Pal From Sydney, Australia

Hi Guys
Never used a chatroom before so here goes.
Fascinating book..quite prescriptive telling us how to design window frames! Pattern Language has been around for so long. It must be a very quite revolution because you never hear of it. I was introduced to it by Warrick Rowell down at Rosneath Farm in Dunsborough, WA. Warrick is a real fanatic about it and is designing the whole built environment on pattern language principles.
As an architect, I am keen to explore the concept of "humanising spaces". Delivering such an outcome through our builder-based construction economy though seems to be a major obstacle.

Pronob Pal 14:47:28 2/18/2002
Wow, it is nice to see some thing with a focus on Australia. Otherwise we feel so left out down-under. However,I am sure these discussion will attract members from all continents.
My main interest with patterns have been on the representation of patterns and in making them part of our lifestyle rather than keeping them a subjective and abstract entity. Surely in that approach we have to be cautious -we should make sure patterns do not become a syntax for writing a piece of software-rather our main focus should be how we can make it easier for people in different walks of life to follow patterns to enhance their life, education,understanding of the nature of things.

Mark Feenstra 14:42:49 2/18/2002
Seeing as I was invited to participate in this conversation I'm assuming the geographical container is Australasia.

My interest in participating is primarily from the perspective of someone wishing to live in a community of people whose physical environment reflects their commitment to learning together about how to live in harmony with the the ground of all being, within the context of a socio-cultural context which largely denies the validity of such a commitment.

I do not have the energy available, given pre-existing commitments, to lead the building project associated with the emergence of such a community, but am actively involved with a group of friends also interested in participating.

I look forward to hearing more about the perspectives and interests of others drawn to contribute to this conversation.
